^DATABASE = GeoMiame
!Database_name = Gene Expression Omnibus (GEO)

^SERIES = GSE161731
!Series_title = Dysregulated transcriptional responses to SARS-CoV-2 in the periphery support novel diagnostic approaches
!Series_geo_accession = GSE161731
!Series_status = Public on Jan 14 2021
!Series_submission_date = Nov 18 2020
!Series_last_update_date = May 25 2021
!Series_pubmed_id = 33597532
!Series_pubmed_id = 34001247
!Series_summary = In order to elucidate novel aspects of the host response to SARS-CoV-2 we performed RNA sequencing on 77 peripheral blood samples across 46 subjects with COVID-19 and compared them to subjects with seasonal coronavirus, influenza, bacterial pneumonia, and healthy controls. The transcriptome in peripheral blood reveals unique aspects of the immune response in COVID-19 and provides for novel biomarker-based approaches to diagnosis.
!Series_overall_design = To define the host peripheral blood transcriptional response in subjects with SARS-CoV-2 infection, we performed RNA sequencing on samples from 46 individuals with PCR-positive, symptomatic SARS-CoV-2 infection, 14 of which were sampled at multiple timepoints. Subjects were enrolled when they presented for clinical care, and the time from symptom onset was recorded for each individual sample collected (range 1-35 days). Subjects with COVID-19 were divided based on disease severity and time from symptom onset (early ≤10 days, middle 11-21 days, late >21 days). As comparators, we profiled banked blood samples from patients presenting to the Emergency Department with acute respiratory infection (ARI) due to seasonal coronavirus (n=59), influenza (n=17) or bacterial pneumonia (n=20), and matched healthy controls (n=19).
!Series_type = Expression profiling by high throughput sequencing
!Series_contributor = Micah,,McClain

!Sample_title = whole blood, 94189
!Sample_geo_accession = GSM4913486
!Sample_status = Public on Jan 14 2021
!Sample_submission_date = Nov 18 2020

!Sample_type = SRA
!Sample_channel_count = 1
!Sample_source_name_ch1 = whole blood
!Sample_organism_ch1 = Homo sapiens
!Sample_taxid_ch1 = 9606
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = subject_id: A1BD46
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = age: 57
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = gender: Female
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = race: Black/African American
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = cohort: Bacterial
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = time_since_onset: NA
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = hospitalized: NA
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = tissue: whole blood
!Sample_characteristics_ch1 = batch: 1
!Sample_molecule_ch1 = polyA RNA
!Sample_extract_protocol_ch1 = Total RNA was extracted from peripheral blood preserved in PAXgene Blood RNA tubes using QIAGEN PAXgene miRNA Extraction Kit according to manufacturer's instructions.
!Sample_extract_protocol_ch1 = Libraries were prepared using NUGEN Universal Plus mRNA-seq with AnyDeplete Globin Kit according to manufacturer's instructions.
!Sample_description = counts_key.csv
!Sample_description = counts.csv
!Sample_description = key.csv
!Sample_description = xpr_nlcpm.csv
!Sample_description = xpr_tpm_geo.txt
!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
!Sample_data_processing = Genome_build: Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83 (Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf and Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa); Reference Download: http://labshare.cshl.edu/shares/gingeraslab/www-data/dobin/STAR/STARgenomes/Old/ENSEMBL/homo_sapiens/ENSEMBL.homo_sapiens.release-83/
!Sample_data_processing = Supplementary_files_format_and_content: counts_key.csv: csv file with demographic information for all samples
!Sample_data_processing = counts.csv: csv file with gene counts for all samples
!Sample_data_processing = key.csv: csv file with demographic information for all samples used in analyses
!Sample_data_processing = xpr_nlcpm.csv: csv file with the TMM normalized expression values on the log2 scale (analysis ready data)
!Sample_data_processing = xpr_tpm_geo.txt: tab-delimited text file with TPM calculated from TMM normalized data

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
!Sample_data_processing = Genome_build: Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83 (Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf and Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa); Reference Download: http://labshare.cshl.edu/shares/gingeraslab/www-data/dobin/STAR/STARgenomes/Old/ENSEMBL/homo_sapiens/ENSEMBL.homo_sapiens.release-83/

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. !Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
!Sample_data_processing = Genome_build: Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83 (Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf and Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa); Reference Download: http://labshare.cshl.edu/shares/gingeraslab/www-data/dobin/STAR/STARgenomes/Old/ENSEMBL/homo_sapiens/ENSEMBL.homo_sapiens.release-83/

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. !Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
!Sample_data_processing = Genome_build: Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83 (Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf and Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa); Reference Download: http://labshare.cshl.edu/shares/gingeraslab/www-data/dobin/STAR/STARgenomes/Old/ENSEMBL/homo_sapiens/ENSEMBL.homo_sapiens.release-83/

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_description = xpr_tpm_geo.txt
!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_description = batch1 raw files: SRR13081356
!Sample_description = batch2 raw files: SRR13081357
!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
!Sample_data_processing = Genome_build: Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83 (Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf and Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa); Reference Download: http://labshare.cshl.edu/shares/gingeraslab/www-data/dobin/STAR/STARgenomes/Old/ENSEMBL/homo_sapiens/ENSEMBL.homo_sapiens.release-83/

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. !Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Generating genome indexes files using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: runMode: genomeGenerate; runThreadN: 16;  genomeDir: path/index; genomeFastaFiles: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.dna.primary_assembly.fa; sjdbGTFfile: path/Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf
!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

!Sample_data_processing = Mapping reads to the genome using STAR v2.7.1a with parameters in the command line: twopassMode: Basic; quantMode: GeneCounts; genomeDir: path/index; runThreadN: 16; readFilesIn: path/sampleid_R1.fastq.gz path/sampleid_R2.fastq.gz; outFileNamePrefix: path/sampleid; readFilesCommand: zcat.
!Sample_data_processing = Genes with counts per million greater than 1 in fewer than 20% of samples were dropped along with three samples that had a high proportion of lowly expressed reads. 
!Sample_data_processing = Data was normalized using the TMM function from the Bioconductor package edgeR.
!Sample_data_processing = Data was log2 transformed
!Sample_data_processing = To get the gene length for calculating TPM, we first extracted transcript information from Homo_sapiens.GRCh38.83.gtf (same reference as STAR) by using the makeTxDbFromGFF function, then collect the exons per gene id using the exonsBy function and for each gene, reduce all the exons to a set of non-overlapping exons, calculate their lengths (widths) and sum them up. Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.

Use the median gene length if there are any duplicates.  Take the TMM normalized counts matrix from previous processing step, use the rpkm function from the to Bioconductor package edgeR v3.28.0 to calculate the RPKM and calculate TPM from RPKM based on the definition. Save the TPM counts matrix for CIBERSORTx analysis.
